?
If the means of production alone cannot explain why you can read, think, and choose belief, then what does that imply about your accountability? Are you living as if you are merely a complex animal driven by material needs, or as a being with a higher calling? What would it look like to fully embrace the responsibility that comes with reason?
?
This lesson exposes the emptiness of any philosophy that reduces human achievements to material causes. Is there an area of your life where you act as if material factors (wealth, status, comfort) are the ultimate drivers of your decisions? How can you realign your priorities to reflect that your intellect and faith come from a non-material source?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
8 min
Refutation of Means of Production as Origin of Development
Buti refutes the claim that means of production are the original cause of all human and animal development.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the materialist claim that means of production are the original cause of all development is self-defeating when comparing human and animal societies.

Core Idea
The same cause cannot produce radically different effects without an explanation.

In this passage, Ramadan Buti takes the materialist philosophy at its word and tests it against observable reality. He points out that if means of production were truly the driving force of all development, then animal societies — which have stronger means of production in the form of claws and fangs — should have developed knowledge, language, and reason just as humans did. The fact that they did not reveals a fatal flaw in the materialist argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp Buti's full argument.
2
Identify the materialist claim
Buti begins by stating the claim he is refuting: that means of production are the original cause of every development. Underline this in the text.
3
Follow the comparison between humans and animals
Notice how Buti points out that means of production exist in both, and are even stronger in animals. Then ask: what would the materialist theory predict?
This sets up the contradiction.
4
Analyze the dilemma
Buti poses a dilemma: if reason is a product of means of production, why did humans submit to its rule and animals not? Reflect on how this undermines the theory.
The dilemma is the core of the refutation.
5
Conclude with the author's verdict
Buti concludes that since materialist philosophy cannot explain this, it is false and lacks proof. Summarize this in your own words.
Remember that Buti is not rejecting material factors entirely, only their claim to be the sole cause.

إن وسيلة الإنتاج التي هي السبب الأصلي لكل تطور وظاهرة في هذا الكون، قد نشأت في تاريخ الإنسان والحيوان معاً. فقد ظهرت في الإنسان بادئ ذي بدء بمظهر اليد والحجارة.. وظهرت في الحيوان بمظهر المخلب والأنياب. ولا شك أنها كانت في الحيوان أقوى منها في الإنسان. فلو كانت هذه الفلسفة صحيحة لنشأ عنها في المجتمع الحيواني مثل الذي نشأ عنها في المجتمع الإنساني من معارف ولغة وعقل ودين ونظم اقتصادية، والأمر كما هو واضح ليس كذلك. إن الفارق الوحيد بين المجتمع الإنساني ودنيا الحيوانات الأخرى، هو فارق العقل والتفكير: وقد ظل هذا الفارق قائماً مع سائر التطورات المختلفة التي لحقت العالم. فإذا كان هذا الفارق نفسه أثراً من آثار القاسم المشترك بين هاتين الخليقتين، وهو «وسيلة الإنتاج»، فكيف تم الخضوع لحكمه في الإنسان فتدرج به إلى المعارف والعقل واللغة والنظم الاجتماعية والاقتصادية، ونشأ التمرد على حكمه في الحيوان فلم يكتسب علماً ولا عقلاً ولا نظاماً؟ وما دامت الفلسفة المادية لا تحدثنا عن سبب ذلك فهي فلسفة باطلة لا يوجد أي دليل على صحتها.
The means of production that are the original cause of every development and phenomenon in this universe have arisen in the history of both man and animal. They appeared in man from the very beginning in the form of the hand and stones, and appeared in the animal in the form of claws and fangs. There is no doubt that they were stronger in the animal than in man. If this philosophy were correct, there would have arisen from it in animal society something like what arose from it in human society of knowledge, language, reason, religion, and economic systems, but the matter, as is clear, is not so. The only difference between human society and the world of other animals is the difference of reason and thought. This difference has remained through all the various developments that have befallen the world. If this very difference is an effect of the common denominator between these two creations, namely the 'means of production,' then how did submission to its rule occur in man, advancing him to knowledge, reason, language, social and economic systems, while rebellion against its rule arose in the animal so that it acquired neither knowledge, nor reason, nor a system? As long as materialist philosophy does not tell us the reason for that, it is a false philosophy for which there exists no proof of its correctness.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the materialist claim that the means of production are the original cause of all development in human society and also in animals. The author begins by stating the materialist premise: the means of production are the primary cause of all development and phenomena in the universe. He then notes that means of production appeared in both humans and animals, but in animals in a stronger form (claws and fangs). If the theory were true, animal societies should have developed the same as human societies—knowledge, language, reason, religion, economic systems—but they did not. The author points out that the only difference between human and animal societies is reason and thought, and this difference persists across all developments. He then poses a dilemma: if this difference (reason) is itself a product of the means of production, why did humans submit to its rule and progress, while animals rebelled and acquired no such progress? Since materialist philosophy cannot explain this discrepancy, it is invalid and lacks proof.

Refuting Economic Determinism with History
Buti refutes economic determinism by noting revolutions occurred in poor, not rich, countries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti refutes the Marxist theory of economic determinism by showing that historical revolutions occurred in economically backward countries, contradicting the theory's predictions.

Core Idea
Revolutions happened where economies were weak, disproving economic determinism.

Buti presents a powerful historical counterexample to the claim that revolutions are caused by economic development. He argues that if the theory were true, revolutions would have first erupted in the richest countries. Instead, they appeared in the poorest. Let's read his precise argument and see how it dismantles a core Marxist assumption.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the English translation. Notice the logical structure: a conditional statement followed by a historical observation.
The passage is short but dense with logical force.
2
Identify the conditional claim
Find the phrase 'if it were true that... then that would require'. This sets up the logical consequence that follows from the Marxist theory.
3
Notice the historical counterexample
Buti then points out what actually happened: revolutions in Russia and China, not in Switzerland or America. This contradicts the conditional's conclusion.
The force of the refutation lies in this factual mismatch.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since the predicted outcome did not occur, the original assumption (economic determinism) is false. The revolution's spark ignited where it should not have, and slept where it should have woken.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum argument.

لو صح أن ازدهار الاقتصاد وتضخم رأس المال هو الذي يقدح زناد الثورة ويسبب انتقال وسائل الإنتاج إلى البروليتاريا، لاستلزم ذلك أن تقوم هذه الثورة في سويسرا وأمريكا ودول أوربا الغربية قبل ظهورها في أي بقعة أخرى من العالم. ولكنها بدلاً من أن تظهر هناك، ظهرت في روسيا والصين وفي عهد كان الاقتصاد فيه ضعيفاً ومتخلفاً. لقد انقدح زناد الثورة حيث كان ينبغي أن لا ينقدح، ونامت عواملها نوماً مستمراً إلى يومنا هذا حيث كان ينبغي أن تستيقظ.
If it were true that the flourishing of the economy and the inflation of capital are what ignite the spark of revolution and cause the transfer of the means of production to the proletariat, then that would require that this revolution occur in Switzerland, America, and Western European countries before its appearance in any other part of the world. But instead of appearing there, it appeared in Russia and China in an era when the economy was weak and backward. The spark of the revolution was ignited where it should not have been ignited, and its factors slept continuously until this day where they should have awoken.

Commentary
This passage is a factual refutation of the Marxist economic determinist claim that revolution occurs when capitalism reaches its peak. The author states the logical consequence of this theory: revolutions should occur first in the most economically developed countries like Switzerland, America, and Western Europe. But history shows the opposite: revolutions happened in backward economies like Russia and China. Therefore, the predicted correlation is false; the revolution ignited where it should not have, and the factors for revolution slept in the developed countries where they should have been active.

The Concept of Acquisition (Kasb) as the Basis of Accountability
Buti defines kasb and refutes the charge of compulsion via legal analogies and Quranic texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine creation of actions does not imply human compulsion because accountability is based on the inner impulse of acquisition (kasb).

Core Idea
Kasb bridges divine creation and human responsibility without coercion.

In this passage, Ramadan al-Buti tackles a key problem in Islamic theology: if God creates all actions, how can humans be accountable? He introduces the concept of kasb (acquisition) as the middle ground. Through legal analogies and Quranic proof, he shows that judgment falls on the inner impulse toward the act, not on the act's created substance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation. Let the flow of analogies and verses settle in your mind.
Notice how Buti begins with a thesis and then supports it with three social examples.
2
Identify the three legal analogies
Find the examples of the car accident, the dug hole, and the poison bottle. For each, ask: who is held accountable, and for what?
Each analogy distinguishes between the direct doer (the car, the workers, the patient) and the acquirer.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Read the four verses Buti cites. Note the consistent use of kasaba/iktasaba. What does this say about the criterion for reward and punishment?
The verses all point to what the person 'earned' or 'acquired', not the act itself.
4
Understand the conclusion
Read the final sentence. How does Buti use kasb to answer the charge that divine creation implies compulsion?
He argues that God's creative power aligns with our impulses, and we are judged on those impulses, not on the created act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ركبها الله في نفسك ) وخلق الفعل وأسبابه القريبة والبعيدة من الله تعالى . وإنما تكون المقاضاة والمحاسبة على القصد والكسب لا على خلق الوسائل والأسباب وخلق الفعل نفسه · وهذه حقيقة نعلمها جميعاً في حياتنا الاجتماعية والقانونية ، فالمقاضاة إنما تكون على الكسب لا على جوهر الفعل المستقل بذاته. إن الذي يدعس بسيارته إنساناً فيقتله ، لا يُقاضى على الفعل ، لأنه ليس هو صاحب الفعل بالذات ، بل صاحب الفعل المباشر هو السيارة نفسها ، ولكنه يُقاضى على الكسب ، والذي جاء بالعمال فحفروا له في قارعة الطريق حوضاً أو بئراً ، لا يعاقب على إفساده للطريق العام لأنه هو الفاعل ، بل لأنه هو الكاسب . والذي جاء بقارورة السم فوضعها في مكان قارورة الدواء التي إلى جانب المريض ، فتناول منها المريض فمات يُقاضى ويقاصَص ، مع أنه ليس هو الفاعل ، ولكنه الكاسب للفعل والمتلبس به . والله عز وجل إنما يقاضي عباده ويحاسبهم ، على هذا الشيء الذي اسمه الكسب ، أي على الانبعاث النفسي إلى التلبس بالفعل ، ألا تلاحظ قوله تعالى : { لا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْساً إلا وُسْعَهَا ، لَها ما كَسَبَتْ وَعَلَيْها مَا اكْتَسَبَتْ } [ البقرة : ٢٨٦ ] وقوله : { اليَوْمَ تُجْزى كُلِّ نَفْسٍ بما كَسَبَتْ } [المؤمن : ١٧ ] وقوله : { وَبَدا لَهُمْ سَيِّئَاتِ ما كَسَبوا } [ الزمر : ٤٨ ] وقوله : { إِنَّ الَّذينَ يكسبون الإثْمَ سَيُجْزَوْنَ بما كانوا يقترفونَ } [الأنعام : ١٢٠ ] إلى ما هنالك من الآيات الكثيرة الأخرى التي تنص على أن مناط الأجر والعقاب إنما هو كسب الإنسان أي انبعاثه نحو الشيء الذي أمر به أو نهي عنه . وإنما شاء الله أن يجعل خلقه وقدرته وفقاً لانبعاثاتهم ، حتى يكون ذلك بمثابة السجل الذي تثبت فيه هذه الانبعاثات مجسدة في مظهر الفعل الذي ظهرت فيه . فقد علمت إذاً أن تعلق صفة الخلق بكل ما قد علم الله وجوده ، فيما لا يزال ، لا يستلزم شيئاً من القسر والجبر المتوهمين
[God] placed in your soul and created the act and its near and distant causes are from God Almighty. Judgment and reckoning are only on intention and acquisition (al-kasb), not on the creation of means and causes and the creation of the act itself. This is a truth we all know in our social and legal life: judgment is only on acquisition, not on the essence of the act independent in itself. The one who runs over a person with his car and kills him is not judged on the act, because he is not the doer (sāḥib al-fi‘l) per se; rather, the direct doer is the car itself, but he is judged on the acquisition (al-kasb). The one who brings workers and they dig a basin or a well for him on the roadside is not punished for corrupting the public road because he is the doer (al-fā‘il), but because he is the acquirer (al-kāsib). The one who brings a poison bottle and places it in the place of the medicine bottle next to the patient, and the patient takes from it and dies, is judged and punished, even though he is not the doer, but he is the acquirer of the act and the one engaged in it. And God Almighty only judges and reckons with His servants on this thing called acquisition (al-kasb), i.e., the psychological impulse to engage in the act. Do you not notice His saying: {Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity; for it is what it has earned (kasabat), and against it is what it has acquired (iktasabat)} [Al-Baqara 2:286], and His saying: {Today every soul will be recompensed for what it has earned (kasabat)} [Ghafir 40:17], and His saying: {And the evils of what they earned (kasabū) will appear to them} [Az-Zumar 39:48], and His saying: {Indeed, those who earn (yaksibūn) evil will be recompensed for what they used to commit} [Al-An‘am 6:120], and many other verses that state that the basis of reward and punishment is only a person's acquisition (kasb)—that is, his impulse toward the thing he is commanded or forbidden. And God willed that His creation and power be in accordance with their impulses, so that that would be like a record in which these impulses are registered embodied in the appearance of the act in which they appear. So you have come to know, then, that the attachment of the attribute of creation (ṣifat al-khalq) to everything that God has known to exist, forever and ever, does not entail anything of the supposed coercion and compulsion (al-qasr wa al-jabr al-mutawahhamayn).
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the concept of 'kasb' (acquisition) as the basis for divine accountability. The author, Ramadān al-Būṭī, begins by affirming that judgment and reckoning are on intention and acquisition, not on the creation of the act itself, which belongs to God. He then provides three everyday legal examples: a driver who accidentally kills is not judged for the act (the car is the direct doer) but for his acquisition (intention/consequence); a person who hires workers to dig a hole is punished not as the direct doer but as the acquirer; a person who swaps poison bottles is judged as the acquirer although not the direct doer. These analogies establish a parallel to divine judgment: God holds people accountable for their inner impulse (inbi‘āth) toward acting, not for the creation of the act. Al-Būṭī then cites four Quranic verses that use derivatives of 'kasb' to argue that reward and punishment are based on what one earns. Finally, he concludes that God's attribute of creation being attached to all existents does not imply any coercion of humans, because the basis of accountability is acquisition, not direct creation.

Key Terms
الكسب (al-kasb)
الانبعاث النفسي (al-inbi‘āth al-nafsī)
جوهر الفعل (jawhar al-fi‘l)
القسر والجبر (al-qasr wa al-jabr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God creates all actions, humans have no real role and are forced (jabr).
Correction: Buti shows that accountability is on the inner acquisition (kasb), not on the created act, preserving human responsibility without denying divine creation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis on which God judges and punishes human beings?
A) The direct act itself, which is created by God
B) The creation of the act, because God is the only doer
C) The acquisition (kasb), i.e., the inner impulse toward the act
D) The outward consequences of the act, regardless of intention

Key Takeaway
Divine judgment is based not on the created act but on the human's inner acquisition (kasb), preserving both God's sovereignty and human responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
If God created every detail of your action, what is left for you to be proud of? Yet the verse {laha ma kasabat} promises reward for your kasb. Will you start seeking reward from the One who values your inner striving, or continue chasing worldly credit?

The Scientific Answer on Causation
Introduces the scientific answer on causation with quotes from Malebranche and William Jones.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the true scientific perspective sees causality as a divine link and why miracles are not rationally inconceivable.

Core Idea
Causality is a divine link, not a natural necessity; miracles are not impossible but reflect divine power.

Before we delve into theological arguments about miracles, we need to address a common objection: that science disproves miracles. But what does science actually say about causation? This lesson presents the answer from two thinkers: philosopher Malebranche and scientist William Jones. They argue that causality is not a necessary connection but a divine mystery, and that miracles are not inconceivable when we understand divine power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once to appreciate its rhetorical style, then read the English translation. Notice how the author builds his argument using two authoritative quotes.
The Arabic is direct; the translation is literal.
2
Identify the two authorities and their arguments
Malebranche argues we only see succession, not the link; the link is divine. William Jones argues that divine power can add or delete, and that what is called 'inconceivable' is relative.
Compare the two arguments: one philosophical, one empirical.
3
Reflect on the implications for miracles
Consider how these quotes counter the claim that miracles are impossible. The key is that causality is not a necessary natural law but a constant divine act.
Think about how this reframes the discussion of miracles in science.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أجل . هذا هو جواب العلم في كلمات مختصرة واضحة . وهو جواب يستطيع أن يسمعه ويعيه كل عاقل أخلص للعلم على وجه الأرض . يقول الفيلسوف مالبرانش : « إنما نرى نحن توالي الحادثات ولا نرى الرابطة التي تربط أحد الطرفين بالآخر ، فلماذا تبقى هذه الرابطة متخفية عنـا ؟ لكونها شيئاً إلهياً لا يوجد مثله في المخلوق » . واسمع ما يقوله العالم الإنكليزي « وليم جونز » : القدرة التي خلقت العالم ، لا تعجز عن حذف شيء منه أو إضافة شيء إليه ، ومن السهل أن يقال عنه : إنه غير متصور عند العقل ، ولكن الذي يقال عنه إنه غير متصور ، ليس غير متصور إلى درجة وجود العالم أي إنه لو لم يكن جزء من هذا العالم موجوداً ، وقيل لـواحد ممن ينكر المعجزات والخوارق ولا يتصور وجودها : سيوجد عالم بالشكل الفلاني ، فإنه سيبادر قائلاً : إن هذا غير متصور ، ويأتي نفيه لذلك أشد من نفي المعجزة التي ينكرها ، مع أنها بعد وجودها لا تحرك شيئاً من الاستغراب أو الدهشة في عقله وينظر إليها دون أن يقول : إن وجود هذا الشيء أمر غير ممكن أو متصور !! ..
Yes. This is the answer of science in clear brief words. And it is an answer that every rational person who is sincere to knowledge on the face of the earth can hear and comprehend. The philosopher Malebranche says: 'We only see the succession of events and we do not see the link that connects one of the two sides to the other. So why does this link remain hidden from us? Because it is a divine thing, the like of which does not exist in creation.' And listen to what the English scientist William Jones says: 'The power that created the world is not incapable of deleting something from it or adding something to it. It is easy to say about it: it is inconceivable to the mind. But what is said to be inconceivable is not inconceivable to the degree of the existence of the world. That is, if a part of this world were not existent, and it were said to one who denies miracles and marvels and does not conceive of their existence: a world of such-and-such form will exist, then he would hasten to say: this is inconceivable. And his denial of that would be stronger than his denial of the miracle he denies, even though after its existence it does not stir any astonishment or wonder in his mind, and he looks at it without saying: the existence of this thing is impossible or inconceivable!! ..
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof by citation. The author begins by stating that the answer of science (i.e., the true scientific perspective) is clear and brief. Anyone sincere to knowledge can understand it. He then quotes two authorities. First, the philosopher Malebranche, who asserts that we only perceive the succession of events, not the causal link between them. The link is hidden because it is divine, not creaturely. Second, the English scientist William Jones argues that God's power is unlimited—He can change the world at will. Jones uses an example: if someone denies miracles and imagines a world missing a part, they would declare that inconceivable, yet their denial is stronger than their denial of a miracle. Yet when the miracle occurs, it doesn't surprise them. This shows that the category of 'inconceivable' is relative, and miracles are not inherently impossible.

Key Terms
الرابطة (al-raabitah: the link)
المعجزات (al-mu'jizaat: miracles)
غير متصور (ghayr mutasawwar: inconceivable)
العلم (al-'ilm: science/knowledge)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Science has proven that causality is a necessary natural law, making miracles impossible.
Correction: The passage shows that science (properly understood) recognizes that we only observe constant conjunction, not necessary connection. The causal link is divine, meaning God directly brings about effects. Miracles are simply unusual acts of divine power, not violations of necessary laws.

Checkpoint
According to Malebranche, why is the causal link between events hidden from us?
A) Because it is a natural law we do not understand.
B) Because it is a divine thing not found in creation.
C) Because our senses are limited.
D) Because we do not observe it closely enough.

Key Takeaway
The true scientific view of causality reveals it as a divine link, so miracles are not impossible but are acts of God's unlimited power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God's power is unlimited, or do you subconsciously limit what He can do based on what you think is 'possible'? What is one area of your life where you have doubted God's ability to intervene, and how does this lesson challenge that doubt?
?
When you see the regular patterns of nature, do you see them as fixed laws or as God's direct action? How would your reliance on God change if you truly saw every event as a divine link rather than a natural necessity?
?
If someone told you that a miracle is 'inconceivable', would you reject it as impossible, or would you remember that many things that exist were once thought inconceivable? In what specific area of your faith are you treating God's power as limited by your own imagination?

Are Miracles Only the Extraordinary? Al-Buti on the True Miracle of Creation
Al-Buti argues that causal regularity is not necessary and all creation is a miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Buti's argument that the regularity of causation is not a necessary law but a constant relationship, and that everything in creation is a miracle.

Core Idea
Causal regularity is not necessity; every moment of existence is a miracle.

Al-Buti challenges the assumption that the laws of nature are fixed and necessary. He argues that what we call causation is merely a pattern we observe, not an unbreakable chain. In this passage, he invites us to see the miraculous in every familiar thing, from planets to our own minds. This shifts the burden of proof: it is not the extraordinary that requires explanation, but the ordinary itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once to get the flow. Notice the rhythm of Al-Buti's argument.
The passage has two main parts: a refutation of necessary causality, then an exhortation to see miracles.
2
Identify the key claim about causality
Al-Buti says the system of causality is 'nothing more than a constant relationship.' What does this imply about the necessity of cause and effect?
He contrasts this with the idea that it must continue necessarily.
3
List the examples of miracles
He lists many examples: planets, movement of spheres, gravity, plants, human mind, nervous system, circulatory system, and man himself. Why does he include so many?
The repetition underscores that familiarity blinds us.
4
Reflect on the critique of familiarity
Al-Buti criticizes those who only consider miracles as violations of the habitual. What is the deeper point about how we judge reality?
He calls it an 'astonishing ignorance' to use what we are used to as a measure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأشياء مما تسميه نظام السببية ليس أكثر من رابطة مطردة تراها بعينك وهيهات أن يكون ذلك مستلزماً لوجوب الاستمرار واستحالة الانفكاك . إن المسبب الأول لا يعجزه شيء عن إبطال هذا التلازم والترابط الصوري الذي تراه . وإن كان طول الإلف واستمرار الاتصال يثير فيك العجب والاستغراب من وقوع ذلك بل العلم يقول لك : إنك لو تأملت ، لرأيت أن المألوف وغير المألوف من مظاهر الكون معجزة في الحقيقة إذا ما غفلت عن ملاحظة الخالق العظيم . فالكواكب معجزة ، وحركة الأفلاك معجزة . وقانون الجاذبية معجزة ، والنباتات معجزة ، والعقل البشري معجزة والمجموعة العصبية في الإنسان معجزة والدورة الدموية فيه معجزة ، والإنسان في ذاته معجزة ! .. غير أنك تنسى - لطول الإلف واستمرار الرؤية - وجه المعجزة في هذا كله ، فتحسب جهلاً وغروراً أن المعجزة ليست إلا تلك التي تفاجئ ما اعتـدتـه وألفتـه بـالمعاكسة والتغيير . ويقول لك العلم : أي قيمة لعقل عاقل يتخذ مما قد اعتاد أن يراه مقياساً لإيمانه بالأشياء وكفر بها ؟.. إنه لجهل عجيب من الإنسان مهما زعم أنه يترقى صعداً في مدارج المدنية والثقافة والفهم
The things we call the system of causality are nothing more than a constant relationship that you see with your own eye, yet far be it that this entails obligatory continuity and impossibility of separation. The First Cause is not incapable of nullifying this apparent correlation and connection that you see. And if prolonged familiarity and continuity of connection arouses in you wonder and astonishment at its occurrence, rather knowledge tells you: if you reflected, you would see that the familiar and unfamiliar manifestations of the universe are a miracle in truth, if you neglect to observe the Great Creator. So the planets are a miracle, the movement of the spheres is a miracle, the law of gravity is a miracle, plants are a miracle, the human mind is a miracle, the nervous system in man is a miracle, the circulatory system in him is a miracle, and man himself is a miracle! ... However, due to prolonged familiarity and continuity of sight, you forget the miraculous aspect in all of this, so you ignorantly and arrogantly reckon that a miracle is only that which surprises what you are accustomed to and familiar with by contradiction and change. And knowledge tells you: what value is there for a rational mind that adopts what it is accustomed to seeing as a measure for its belief in things and its disbelief in them? It is an astonishing ignorance of man, no matter how much he claims to ascend in the ranks of civilization, culture, and understanding.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a combined refutation and exhortation. Al-Buti first refutes the notion that causal regularity is a necessary law by stating that what we call causality is merely a constant relationship we observe, not a necessary connection. The First Cause (God) can annul it. He then shifts to an exhortation: if we reflect, everything in creation is a miracle, but familiarity blinds us. He lists examples: planets, spheres, gravity, plants, mind, nervous system, circulation, and man himself. He criticizes those who limit miracles to violations of the familiar and who use familiarity as a measure of belief. This is a direct attack on naturalism and a call to see the divine hand in all things.

Key Terms
نظام السببية
المسبب الأول
معجزة
الإلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The regularity of cause and effect is a necessary, unbreakable law.
Correction: Al-Buti shows that it is merely a constant relationship that God can annul at any time; thus it is not necessary.

Key Takeaway
Al-Buti teaches that the regularity of nature is not a necessary law but a pattern sustained by God, and that familiarity blinds us to the miracle present in all of creation.

?
You may claim to believe in God's power, but do your daily thoughts and reactions reflect that belief, or do you act as if nature runs on its own? What would change in your attitude if you truly lived each moment as a direct act of God?

Empirical Evidence of the Universe's Service to Humans
Buti presents the second rational argument using empirical observation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti uses empirical observation of cosmic order as a rational proof for divine purpose and human nobility.

Core Idea
The universe is arranged around human needs—this intentional order points to a Creator.

In this passage, Buti shifts from logical deduction to empirical observation. He presents a second rational argument: the observable fact that the entire cosmos—from celestial motions to earthly functions—serves human needs. This teleological coherence, he argues, reveals a purposeful design and elevates humans as the central purpose of creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once silently, then read the English translation. Notice the Quranic verse embedded in the argument.
2
Identify the three components of the argument
Buti builds his case with: (a) the Quranic verse about subjection, (b) empirical observation of cosmic service, (c) the conclusion about human nobility. Mark each part.
The verse serves as both a revealed truth and a promise that empirical evidence confirms.
3
Understand the 'pole of the circle' analogy
Reflect on the image of man as the axis around which all other existents revolve. What does this imply about purpose and intention?
This is a key metaphor: the universe's movement is not random but centered on human wellbeing.
4
Connect observation to conclusion
How does Buti move from 'the universe serves humans' to 'humans are the noblest beings'? Trace the logical implication.
The service of all things implies they are subordinate, and the served is superior.
5
Review the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to test your grasp of the evidence used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأمر الثاني : مانراه بالتجربة والمشاهدة من دلائل صدق قول الله تعالى : وسَخَّرَ لَكُم ما في السَّمواتِ ومَا في الأرض جميعاً مِنهُ ﴾ [ الجاثية : ١٣ ] فأنت ترى أن كلاً من حركة الفلك ونظام الكون ووظائف المكونات المختلفة - إنما يجري وفقاً لحاجة الإنسان وخدمته ، فالإنسان يُمثّل في هذا الوجود الذي من حوله قطب الدائرة ، على حين ينجذب إليه مختلف الموجودات الأخرى في تطواف دائب وسعى مستمر لتنسج له مقومات الحياة الفضلى وتهيئ له متطلبـاتـه وحاجاته المختلفة
ومن لوازم ذلك ) كما ترى ) أن يغدو هذا الكائن الذي هذا شأنه مع سائر الموجودات ، وشأن سائر الموجودات معه - أفضلها وأشرفها على الإطلاق
The second matter: What we see through experience and observation of the proofs of the truth of God's saying: {And He has subjected to you whatever is in the heavens and whatever is in the earth, all from Him} [Al-Jathiyah 13]. So you see that each of the motion of the celestial sphere and the system of the cosmos and the functions of the various components is only conducted according to the need of man and his service. So man represents in this existence around him the pole of the circle, while the various other existents are attracted to him in a constant rotation and continuous effort to weave for him the components of the best life and prepare for him his needs and various necessities. And from the consequences of that, as you see, is that this being whose condition is this with regard to other existents, and the condition of other existents with regard to him, becomes the best and most noble of them absolutely.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents the second rational argument based on empirical observation. The author points to the verse from Surah Al-Jathiyah that states God has subjected everything in the heavens and earth to humans. He then argues that we can observe that the motion of celestial bodies, the order of the cosmos, and the functions of all components are arranged according to human needs and service. Humans are the center (pole) of the circle, with all other things revolving around them to provide the best life and meet their needs. The conclusion is that humans are the best and most noble of all existents. This argument relies on the observable teleological design of the universe.

Correction: Buti includes the entire cosmic order—celestial motions and system of the cosmos—as serving humans, implying a purpose beyond mere utility.

Lamarck's Theory of Evolution
Buti presents Lamarck's theory of evolution and its proposed mechanism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core claims of Lamarckism, including its mechanism of adaptation and the examples cited by Lamarck.

Core Idea
Lamarckism explains species change as a response to environmental circumstances over time.

Dr. Buti begins by presenting Lamarck's theory as one of the earliest and most important theories of evolution. He explains its mechanism: changing circumstances alter habits, which over time change functions and organs. Lamarck supported this with examples like atrophied teeth and the mole's eyes. This lesson unpacks that theory and its initial acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Read the theory presentation
Read the Arabic passage once without focusing on details. Then read the translation. Notice the narrative flow from birth to growth to decline.
The passage uses a metaphor of birth, growth, and regression.
2
Identify the mechanism chain
Lamarck proposes a chain: circumstances → habits → functions → organs. Find each link in the passage and how it connects with 'affects'.
Look for words like 'يؤثر' and 'مع الاستمرار' and 'مع الزمن'.
3
Examine the supporting examples
Lamarck gives three examples: vertebrates with atrophied teeth, whale and anteater, and the mole's eyes. Notice how each illustrates the chain.
These examples are meant to show the results of habit changes over time.
4
Observe the theory's initial reception
The passage notes that Lamarck's analysis initially had little success but later gained popularity. Reflect on why a theory might gain acceptance despite limited evidence.
This sets up the later refutation in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلنستعرض أهم هذه النظريات، ولنتأمل كيفية ولادة كل منها، ثم كيفية نموه في حقل الأدلة التي اعتمد عليها، ثم رجوعه القهقرى إلى حيث الضلالة والضعف، تحت وطأة النقض والنقد اللذين تسارعا إليه من كل جانب. اللاماركية: ولعل من أسبق هذه النظريات وأهمها ما نادى به العالم التصنيفي لامارك من أن عدم ثبات الأنواع على حالها إنما يعود إلى الظروف المختلفة التي تتقلب على كل منها، كالإقليم أو الغذاء أو طراز الحياة أو طبيعة المناخ إلخ. فاختلاف شيء من هذه الظروف يؤثر في اختلاف العادات، واختلاف العادات يؤثر - مع الاستمرار - في اختلاف الوظائف والأعمال، واختلافهما يؤثر - مع الزمن - في اختلاف الشكل والأعضاء. ولقد دعم لامارك نظريته هذه بعدد من الأمثلة الحية التي استرعت انتباهه، فالفقاريات التي تتغذى بدون مضغ تضمر أسنانها وتصبح خفية في اللثتين. والحوت وآكل النمل مثالان على ذلك. والخلد الذي يعيش في الظلام يتمتع بعينين صغيرتين جداً لا تكادان تنهضان بوظيفة. وعلى الرغم من أن هذا التحليل الذي تقدم به لامارك، كتفسير لما فرضه من آلية التطور، لم ينل في البدء إلا قليلاً من النجاح، فإنه راح يشع فيما بعد في أذهان الناس، وراحوا يعتبرونه، إلى حين من الزمن، خير تفسير لظاهرة التطور. والتصقت النظرية باسم صاحبها، فراحوا يطلقون عليها: اللاماركية. ولكن ما إن وضعت النظرية تحت مجهر البحث والنقد ودلائل التجربة والاستقراء، حتى انطفأ شعاعها وانكفأت على أعقابها وتقلص ما كان لها من سلطان على الأذهان. نقد اللاماركية: ولنعدد الآن بعض الانتقادات التي وجهت إليها:
Let us then review the most important of these theories, and contemplate how each was born, then how it grew in the field of evidence it relied upon, then its regression backwards into error and weakness under the weight of refutation and criticism that hastened to it from every side. Lamarckism: Perhaps among the earliest and most important of these theories is that proclaimed by the taxonomist Lamarck: that the instability of species in their state is due to the different circumstances that change upon each of them, such as region, food, lifestyle, or nature of climate, etc. So variation in any of these circumstances affects variation in habits, and variation in habits – with continuity – affects variation in functions and actions, and variation of the two – with time – affects variation in form and organs. Lamarck supported his theory with a number of living examples that caught his attention: vertebrates that feed without chewing have atrophied teeth that become hidden in the gums; the whale and the anteater are two examples of that; and the mole that lives in darkness has very small eyes that hardly perform a function. And although this analysis put forward by Lamarck, as an interpretation of the mechanism of evolution he assumed, initially achieved only little success, it began later to radiate in people's minds, and they began to consider it, for a time, the best interpretation of the phenomenon of evolution. The theory became attached to the name of its author, and they began to call it: Lamarckism. But as soon as the theory was placed under the microscope of research, criticism, and the evidences of experiment and induction, its radiance was extinguished, it retreated on its heels, and its hold over minds shrank. Critique of Lamarckism: Now let us list some of the criticisms that were directed against it:
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is an exposition and evaluation of Lamarckism. The author first introduces the need to review the major theories of evolution, observing their birth, growth, and subsequent decline under criticism. He then presents Lamarckism: it posits that species are not fixed; change is due to differing circumstances (region, food, lifestyle, climate). These affect habits, which long-term affect functions, and eventually form and organs. Lamarck supported this with examples: atrophied teeth in vertebrates that don't chew, the whale and anteater, and the mole's small eyes. Initially the theory had limited success but later gained popularity as the best explanation of evolution. It became known as Lamarckism. However, when subjected to rigorous research, experiment, and induction, its influence faded and it was refuted. The author concludes by signaling an upcoming enumeration of specific criticisms, though the actual list is not included in this window. The passage is a historical and critical overview of Lamarck's theory, showing its rise and fall.

اللاماركية
التطور
الثبات
الظروف
الاستمرار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary cause of species variation in Lamarck's theory?
A) Random genetic mutations
B) Different circumstances affecting habits and organs over time
C) Natural selection by predators
D) Divine intervention

Key Takeaway
Lamarck proposed that environmental changes cause habit changes, which through continuity and time lead to changes in form and organs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The theory of Lamarckism gained popularity despite weak beginnings. Think of a belief you once held because it was widely accepted, only to later realize it was flawed. How will you ensure that you base your convictions on truth rather than popularity, especially in matters of faith?
?
Lamarck proposed that continuous habits shape one's physical form. Consider your daily habits — prayers, thoughts, actions. Over time, what kind of 'spiritual form' are they shaping in you? Is it the form you want to present before Allah?
?
The mole's eyes became small because they were not used. Are there aspects of your faith or character that have atrophied because you have neglected them? What will you do today to revive them?

The Refutation of Lamarckism
Buti narrates the decline of Lamarckism under scientific scrutiny and introduces criticisms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Lamarckism was refuted by scientific evidence and criticism, leading to its decline.

Core Idea
Lamarckism's radiance was extinguished when put under the microscope of research and experiment.

Dr. Buti now describes the fate of Lamarck's theory: after initial popularity, it was subjected to rigorous research and criticism, which led to its refutation and decline. This lesson examines the decline and the specific criticisms that were leveled against it, as promised by the author.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the imagery of light extinguished and retreat.
The author uses metaphorical language like 'shining' and 'extinguished'.
2
Identify the factors that led to refutation
The passage mentions 'research, criticism, experiment, and induction' as the means that disproved the theory. Reflect on why these are powerful tools.
These are the same tools used in Islamic kalam for testing claims.
3
Understand the promise of specific criticisms
The author says 'let us list some of the criticisms'. This signals that details will follow. Note the structure: first the general decline, then specific points.
The actual list may be in subsequent lessons.
4
Reflect on the lesson for epistemology
This passage shows how even widely accepted theories can be overturned by evidence. Think about the importance of skepticism and verification.
This connects to the broader theme of certainty in Islamic thought.

This passage is an exposition and evaluation of Lamarckism. The author first introduces the need to review the major theories of evolution, observing their birth, growth, and subsequent decline under criticism. He then presents Lamarckism: it posits that species are not fixed; change is due to differing circumstances (region, food, lifestyle, climate). These affect habits, which long-term affect functions, and eventually form and organs. Lamarck supported this with examples: atrophied teeth in vertebrates that don't chew, the whale and anteater, and the mole's small eyes. Initially the theory had limited success but later gained popularity as the best explanation of evolution. It became known as Lamarckism. However, when subjected to rigorous research, experiment, and induction, its influence faded and it was refuted. The author concludes by signaling an upcoming enumeration of specific criticisms, though the actual list is not included in this window. The passage is a historical and critical overview of Lamarck's theory, showing its rise and fall.

Correction: The passage suggests it was a combination of research, criticism, experiment, and induction that led to its decline.

The Limitations of Lamarckism in Explaining Evolution
Buti critiques Lamarckism for its limited explanatory scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Buti argues that Lamarckism cannot account for the complete qualitative transformation of animal species.

Core Idea
Lamarckism only explains partial changes, not the full evolutionary transformation.

In this passage, Buti critiques Lamarckism by highlighting its narrow scope. He first points to genetic evidence that organism structure is intrinsic, not environmentally determined. Then he argues that even if Lamarckism were valid, it only covers minor adjustments, not the holistic change required for a complete theory of evolution.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation to grasp Buti's two main arguments: the genetic rebuttal and the scope limitation.
2
Identify the two critiques
Note that Buti first dismisses Lamarckism based on genetics, then argues that even apart from that, it only addresses a smaller question.
3
Reflect on the key phrase 'تجاوب وانسجام'
This term 'correspondence and harmony' is crucial: Buti says there is no harmony between environmental conditions and the complete qualitative revolution needed.

(۱) بالظروف والأحوال سيما وقد تبين من علم الوراثة أن الهيكل الأساسي للكائن الحي ليس من العوامل الخارجية وإنما هو أصل ذاتي حسب اقتران الصبغيات والناسلات لكل نوع وحده . ودعوى أن الأمر لم يكن على هذا النحو الوراثي في غابر الأزمان السحيقة ، زعم غيبي بحت يتنافى مع الواقع المستمر المشاهد
(۲) ثالثاً ـ وبقطع النظر عن كل نقد يوجه إلى هذه الفرضية ، فإنها تعالج مسألة أخرى أضيق بكثير من موضوع بحثنا الشامل الذي يتناول تحليل فرضية تقول بتطور الحيوان تطوراً نوعياً كاملاً لا يحده تبدل أشكال وألوان وأعضاء من الحيوان ، بل يأتي على التكوين الحيواني كله ، بدءاً من الغريزة والفكر ، إلى الشكل والشعر والمخالب والأظفار ، ضمن ظروف لا يتراءى بينها وبين هذا الانقلاب النوعي أي تجاوب وانسجام .
فالتحليل الذي تذهب إليه النظرية اللاماركية بالنسبة لظاهرة الأشكال والأعضاء الجزئية التى تتأثر مع الزمن بحال البيئة والظروف والأجواء ، لاتغطى إلا جزءاً يسيراً جداً من موضوع البحث الأساسي ، الذي لايزال يتطلب تحليلاً وشرحاً يجيبان على أسئلة كثيرة تفرض نفسها في هذا المجال
(1) [He speaks] about circumstances and conditions, especially since genetics has demonstrated that the basic structure of the living organism is not from external factors but is an intrinsic origin according to the pairing of chromosomes and [؟] for each species alone. And the claim that the matter was not in this hereditary manner in the remote past ages is a purely occult assertion that contradicts the continuous observable reality.
(2) Thirdly - and apart from any criticism directed to this hypothesis, it treats another question much narrower than our comprehensive research topic, which deals with the analysis of a hypothesis that posits a complete qualitative evolution of the animal, not limited to a change of forms, colors, and organs of the animal, but rather encompasses the entire animal constitution, beginning from instinct and intellect, to form, hair, claws and nails, within conditions in which no correspondence or harmony is perceived between them and this qualitative revolution.
So the analysis that the Lamarckian theory goes to regarding the phenomenon of partial forms and organs that are affected over time by the state of the environment, conditions, and climates, covers only a very small part of the fundamental research topic, which still requires analysis and explanation that answer many questions that impose themselves in this area.

Commentary
This passage critiques Lamarckism by highlighting its limited scope. Buti begins by noting that genetics reveals the basic structure of organisms is intrinsic, determined by chromosomes and [؟] for each species, not by external factors. Claims that hereditary inheritance was different in the distant past are unscientific conjecture contradicting observable reality. In the second section (marked 'Thirdly'), he states that even aside from criticism, Lamarckism addresses a much narrower problem than the full qualitative evolution of animals—a transformation that covers not just superficial traits (form, color, organs) but the entire constitution (instinct, intellect, hair, claws). The Lamarckian analysis of partial changes due to environment accounts for only a small fraction of this fundamental issue, leaving many unanswered questions.

Darwinism and Natural Selection Explained
Buti presents Darwin's theory of evolution by natural selection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti presents Darwin's theory of evolution by natural selection, its derivation from Malthus, and the mechanical explanation it offers.

Core Idea
Darwin's natural selection is a mechanical cause, not a goal-driven one.

Buti now turns to address Darwinism, a modern theory that attempts to explain biological diversity without recourse to purpose or design. He outlines its core mechanism — natural selection — and traces its intellectual roots to Malthusian population theory. This presentation sets the stage for a subsequent critique from an Islamic theological perspective.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting how Buti introduces Darwin's project as a mechanical explanation.
2
Identify the Malthusian link
Notice that Darwin derived his idea from Malthus's principle of population growth vs. food supply, which leads to competition.
3
Examine the evidence and conclusion
Look at the elephant example as evidence for natural selection, and note the resulting hierarchy of species.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الداروينية :
في عام ١٨٧١ أخرج داروين كتابه المشهور المسمى بـ « أصل الأنواع والانتخاب بالنسبة للجنس » حاول فيه أن يردّ التطور إلى تفسير آلي بحت . بحيث يكون مستقلاً قدر الإمكان عن الأسباب الغائية ولكنه مع ذلك اتخذ من مبدأ اختيار الأصلح سبباً للتطور .
وقد استمد داروین نظريته من كتاب « السكان » للاقتصادي المعروف مالتوس ، الذي كان يزعم بأن السكان يزدادون بنسبة هندسية بينما لا تزداد نسبة الغذاء إلا بنسبة حسابية ، مما يؤدي إلى تنافس وتنازع بين الأفراد على الغذاء ليتلاشى غير الأكفاء
فهو يرى أن ثمة صفات ، قد لا تكون ذات أهمية في الظاهر ، يتفاوت الأفراد في مدى اتصافهم بها ، يكون لها أثر فعال في المحافظة على صاحبها وترشيحه لمستوى أفضل . وعندما يدخل هؤلاء الأفراد في صراع مع الطبيعة من أجل الحياة يجري اصطفاء طبيعي يؤدي إلى بقاء أشد الأفراد كفاءة وصلاحية للبقاء ، بما تمتاز به من تلك الصفات ، أو بما تمتاز به من الحصول على أعلى الرتب منها
ويستشهد داروين على أحقية هذا الاصطفاء بتلك العوامل الهائلة . التي تبيد نتاج كثير من الكائنات الحية مع الزمن . فهو يلفت نظرنا مثلاً إلى أن أنثى الفيل تضع خلال حياتها ستة صغار ، ولو اتبعنا هذا الأساس فإنه يجب أن نتاج كل ذكر واحد وأنثى واحدة في نهاية سبعمائة وخمسين عاماً نحو تسعة عشر مليوناً . وواضح جداً أن الواقع الطبيعي بعيد كل البعد عن هذا الحساب
وهكذا فإن التفوق الذي يتمتع به الحيوان ، من حيث هو نوع بالنسبة للأنواع الأخرى ، أو من حيث هو فرد بالنسبة للأفراد الأخرى يمكنه من اكتساح غيره لا في أصل الوجود فحسب بل في خصائص الوجود أيـضـاً ومـا قـد ينطوي عليه من تعقيدات مفيدة
وفي غمرة هذا التسابق الذي تم منذ أقدم العصور في عالم الأحياء ، ونتيجة لتفاوت الصفات الكامنة في كل منها - وهي الطاقة الوحيدة لذلك التسابق - ظهر سلم الدرجات التي صنفت هذه الأحياء إلى أنواع مختلفة ومتفـاوتـة شتى . وليس
Darwinism:
In the year 1871, Darwin published his famous book called 'The Origin of Species and Selection in Relation to Sex' in which he attempted to reduce evolution to a purely mechanical explanation. So that it be as independent as possible from final causes, but nevertheless he adopted the principle of the survival of the fittest as a cause for evolution.
He derived his theory from the book 'Population' by the well-known economist Malthus, who claimed that populations increase in geometric ratio while the food supply increases only in arithmetic ratio, leading to competition and struggle among individuals for food, so that the unfit disappear.
So he sees that there are qualities, perhaps not important in appearance, in which individuals vary in the extent of their possession, which have an effective impact in preserving their possessor and recommending him for a better level. And when these individuals enter into a struggle with nature for life, a natural selection occurs that leads to the survival of the most efficient and fit individuals, by virtue of those qualities, or by virtue of obtaining the highest ranks of them.
And Darwin cites as evidence for the validity of this selection those immense factors that destroy the offspring of many living organisms over time. For example, he draws our attention to the fact that the female elephant gives birth during her life to six young, and if we follow this principle, then from one male and one female, after seven hundred and fifty years, there should be about nineteen million. And it is very clear that natural reality is far from this calculation.
Thus, the superiority that an animal enjoys, whether as a species over other species, or as an individual over other individuals, enables it to sweep away others not only in the origin of existence but also in the characteristics of existence and what it may contain of useful complexities.
And in the midst of this race that has taken place since the earliest times in the world of living beings, and as a result of the variation of the inherent qualities in each of them—and it is the sole energy of that race—the ladder of degrees appeared that classified these living beings into various and diverse species.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents Darwin's theory of evolution by natural selection. Buti begins by noting Darwin's 1871 book 'The Descent of Man and Selection in Relation to Sex' (though the title cited is slightly different), in which Darwin attempted to explain evolution mechanically, independent of teleological causes, using the principle of survival of the fittest. He then explains the Malthusian influence: population grows geometrically while food supply grows arithmetically, causing competition. Individuals possess varying traits; those with advantageous traits survive and reproduce (natural selection). As evidence, Darwin gives the elephant example: if all offspring survived, numbers would skyrocket, but reality shows many perish. The result is a hierarchy of species based on differential success in the struggle for existence.

اختيار الأصلح

مالتوس

Misconception: Darwin's theory requires no goal or purpose; it is a purely mechanical process.
Correction: While Darwin attempted a mechanical explanation, the passage shows he still used teleological language like 'survival of the fittest' and 'useful complexities', leaving room for critique.

Key Takeaway

Introduction and First Criticism of Darwinism
Author introduces critique and gives first argument: reality contradicts Darwin's law.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first critique of Darwin's theory of natural selection: that the persistence of weak and primitive species contradicts the law of survival of the fittest.

Core Idea
Darwin's 'survival of the fittest' fails to explain why primitive species still thrive.

In this passage, the author begins his critique of Darwinism by focusing on a key empirical observation: the continued existence of weak, primitive species. He argues that this directly contradicts Darwin's proposed law of natural selection. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the author's introduction to his critique of Darwinism.
Notice the author's use of enumeration to structure his criticisms.
2
Identify the first criticism
Focus on the first numbered point: what does the author claim contradicts Darwin's law? He observes that weak and primitive species still exist abundantly.
The criticism is that reality should show only fittest species if the law were true.
3
Understand the logic
The author uses a logical argument: if Darwin's law were correct, primitive species would have been eliminated by now. Since they haven't, the law is contradicted.
This is a modus tollens: if P then Q, not Q, therefore not P.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider what this criticism means for the theory of evolution by natural selection. Does it completely refute Darwinism, or does it point to a need for revision?
The author presents this as one of many criticisms, not necessarily a fatal blow.

Critique of Darwinism: Dr. Abd al-Halim Suwaydan says: The Darwinian theory has aroused much criticism. Then he presented a group of them and said about them afterwards that they are a small part of many other criticisms directed at Darwinism. So let us enumerate, quickly, these criticisms and others, taking into consideration what Darwin himself directed against his theory of problems, for many of which he admitted they are intractable problems and sufficed with that without attempting to solve them or answer them!...

1- The reality we witness sharply contradicts what Darwin called the law of selection and survival of the fittest. For the universe still - after all its long age - teems with the fittest, the fit, and the unfit from all kinds of animals, beginning from jellyfish to monkeys to humans!... And if his law were correct, one of its simplest clear requirements would be that the procession of the animal race would have passed the starting point at the very least, no matter how slow we assume the movement of evolution and selection. But here is the starting point still teeming with its weak, backward animals, and they still enjoy their lives and living characteristics just as the predecessors enjoyed, exactly alike. (1)
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to a critique of Darwinism, followed by the first argument. The author quotes Dr. Abd al-Halim Suwaydan, who begins by noting that Darwin's theory has faced much criticism. He then declares his intention to enumerate some of these criticisms, including those admitted by Darwin himself as intractable. The first criticism is that empirical reality contradicts Darwin's law of survival of the fittest. The author points out that despite the supposed progress of evolution, weak and primitive species (such as jellyfish) still exist in large numbers. If Darwin's law were correct, these primitive forms should have been eliminated long ago; yet they persist just as they always have. This undermines the claim that only the fittest survive.

Chance vs. Selection in Nature
The author argues that death and survival are often due to chance, not natural selection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second criticism of Darwinism: that death and survival in nature are often due to random chance rather than natural selection.

Core Idea
Nature's disasters kill indiscriminately — chance, not fitness, decides who lives.

This lesson examines a key objection to Darwin's theory of natural selection. The author argues that while species certainly suffer losses, these losses are frequently caused by unpredictable events that do not favor the fittest. Through vivid examples, we see that death or survival often comes down to sheer luck, not superior traits.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice how the author sets up a common observation, then introduces a contrasting explanation.
The passage cites Dr. Abd al-Halim Suwaydan.
2
Identify the main claim
Find the sentence that states the core argument: that death and survival are often due to sheer chance, not special qualities.
Look for 'إن كلاً من الموت والنجاة من الموت كثيراً ما يكون عائداً إلى المصادفة المجردة'.
3
Analyze the examples
Examine the two examples: the drying marsh and the huge wave. How do they illustrate the point that selection is not at work?
Both examples show indiscriminate killing and survival.
4
Contrast with natural selection
Notice how the author contrasts the common view (selection of the fittest) with the reality of chance events. Why is this a serious criticism of Darwinism?
The criticism challenges the idea that competition is the main driver of evolution.
5
Summarize the criticism
In your own words, restate the second criticism. This will help solidify your understanding.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢ - لا خلاف في أن كل نوع من الحيوانات تطرأ عليه خسائر ضخمة مع الزمن بسبب عوادٍ وعوامل طبيعية مختلفة تتغلب عليها . هذه حقيقة مشاهدة لا تنكر . أما أن تكون الكارثة نتيجة تسابق وتنافس ينتهيان باصطفاء الأنسب والأقدر فهذه ـ كما يقول الدكتور عبد الحليم سويدان - مسألة أخرى ... إن كلاً من الموت والنجاة من الموت كثيراً ما يكون عائداً إلى المصادفة المجردة لا إلى صفات خاصة في الفرد . فالمستنقع العظيم الذي يجف والموجة الهائلة التي تتدفق على الرمل ، يتركان بعدهما ألوفاً من الجثث ، وتنجو من كارثة الموت طائفة أخرى ، ولكن لا الموت اصطفى لنفسه الضعفاء ولا النجاة اختارت لنفسها الأقوياء ، بل الأمر كله جاء على سبيل المصادفة
2- There is no dispute that every species of animals incurs huge losses over time due to various natural calamities and factors that overcome them. This is an observable fact that cannot be denied. But that the disaster is a result of competition and rivalry ending in selection of the most suitable and most capable - this, as Dr. Abd al-Halim Suwaydan says, is another matter... Indeed, both death and escape from death are often due to sheer chance, not to special qualities in the individual. So the great marsh that dries up and the huge wave that flows onto the sand leave behind thousands of corpses, and another group escapes from the disaster of death, but death did not select the weak for itself, nor did survival choose the strong for itself, rather the whole matter came about by chance.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents the second criticism of Darwinism. The author argues that while it is true that species suffer large losses over time, these losses are often due to unpredictable natural events rather than competitive selection. He gives examples of a drying marsh and a flood wave: both kill indiscriminately, not based on fitness. Some die, some survive, but neither death nor survival is selective. This shows that chance, not natural selection, is often the determining factor in who lives and who dies.

Third Criticism: Death and the Survival of the Fittest
The author argues that death contradicts Darwin's law of progress through selection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fact of death contradicts Darwin's principle of survival of the fittest, and how statistical evidence undermines his predictions.

Core Idea
Death targets the exceptional, not the average — the opposite of survival of the fittest.

In this third criticism, the author turns Darwin's own logic against him. Darwin claimed that nature selects the fittest for survival. But if death is universal and often strikes the most exceptional individuals first, then how can the fittest be said to survive? The author presents statistical studies that show this exact pattern, directly contradicting Darwin's theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the criticism carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the rhetorical question that challenges Darwin's idea.
The author uses a simple but powerful question to highlight the contradiction.
2
Identify the main claim
The author argues that death itself contradicts the law of selection and preservation of the fittest. Death lies in wait for all, including the fittest.
3
Consider the statistical evidence
The author cites statistical studies showing that death attacks above-average individuals first, leaving the average and below to survive. This is the opposite of Darwin's prediction.
This empirical evidence is crucial to the argument.
4
Reflect on the contradiction
Understand that the pattern described directly undermines Darwin's theory. Instead of preserving the fittest, nature often eliminates them first.

This is the opposite of what Darwin's theory would predict—instead of the fittest being preserved, they are often eliminated first.

Selection Demands Purpose and Intelligence
The author argues that selection involves purpose, not blind mechanism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the process of selection—whether natural or artificial—cannot be purely mechanical or random but must involve purpose and intelligence, pointing to a Creator.

Core Idea
Selection implies purpose, and purpose requires intelligence—nature alone cannot explain it.

The author presents the fourth criticism against the idea that nature operates blindly through selection. He argues that any selection process, by its very nature, aims at an end goal. Striving toward a goal is one of the most complex acts of understanding, and it cannot be attributed to a mindless nature that acts only mechanically or randomly. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the logical flow: first, selection is not mechanical; second, it requires a law to distinguish the fittest.
The passage is short but dense—take your time.
2
Identify the key claim
The author states that selection is 'a means that aims at an end.' This is the central thesis. Reflect on why goal-directedness implies intelligence.
Contrast this with blind mechanisms like gravity or chemical reactions.
3
Examine the second paragraph
The author asks: on what law does nature base its election of the fittest? Consider the implication: without a conscious law, natural selection would be arbitrary.
This question challenges the coherence of natural selection as a mindless process.
4
Connect to the broader argument
This criticism is part of a larger case for the existence of God. Understand how the need for purpose and law points to a purposeful Creator.
The author assumes that purpose cannot arise from purposelessness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - إن عملية الاصطفاء ليست حركة آلية ، سواء اعتبرناها اصطفاء صنعياً أو طبيعياً ، بل هي وسيلة تستهدف غاية . والسعي نحو غاية ما يعتبر أعقد عمليات الفهم والإدراك . فكيف يمكن إسناد ذلك إلى « الطبيعة » التي لا مناص من تفسير عملها وآثارها ، مهما تنوعت التعابير عنها ، بالآلية أو العشوائية المجردة

4- The process of selection is not a mechanical movement, whether we consider it artificial or natural selection, rather it is a means that aims at an end. So how can that be attributed to 'nature' which can only be interpreted, however diverse the expressions about it, as mechanistic or sheer randomness?

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth criticism. The author argues that selection—whether artificial or natural—cannot be a purely mechanical process because it inherently involves goal-directedness (teleology). Striving towards an end requires intelligence and understanding, which cannot be attributed to a nature that is merely mechanistic or random. In the second paragraph, he presses further: selecting the fittest requires a law that distinguishes the fittest and provides a rationale. If nature is blind, it cannot possess such a law. Thus, the very concept of selection implies a purposeful agent, not blind chance.

Buti presents the fifth criticism: nature would prevent weak life if it could.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
If nature controlled selection, it would prevent weakness, not tolerate it.

This lesson examines the fifth criticism leveled against the claim that nature is the agent behind the order of life. The author argues that if nature truly had the power to select, it would be far easier for it to block weak individuals from existing at all, rather than allowing them to enter life and then participate in functions. This inconsistency undermines the notion of nature as a selective force.

Selection Requires Purpose, Not Blind Nature
Fourth argument: natural selection implies goal-directed agency, not blind automatism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the process of selection cannot be purely mechanical or random but must involve goal-directed agency.

Core Idea
Selection requires purpose and law, not blind nature.

This lesson presents a powerful argument against reducing natural selection to a blind, mechanical process. The author argues that selection, whether artificial or natural, is inherently goal-directed and requires a law to distinguish the fittest. How could blind nature possibly fulfill these conditions?

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the rhetorical questions the author poses.
The passage is compact and argumentative.
2
Identify the two claims
The author makes two key claims: (1) selection is goal-directed, not automatic; (2) selection requires a law to distinguish the fittest. Find these in the text.
3
Consider the implications
Reflect on why goal-directedness cannot be attributed to nature, which is mechanical or random. What would nature need to have to perform selection?
This challenges a common assumption.
4
Engage with the rhetorical questions
The author ends with two questions. Try to answer them from the perspective of a naturalistic worldview.
These questions expose the incoherence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ - إن عملية الاصطفاء ليست حركة آلية ، سواء اعتبرناها اصطفاء صنعياً أو طبيعياً ، بل هي وسيلة تستهدف غاية . والسعي نحو غاية ما يعتبر أعقد عمليات الفهم والإدراك . فكيف يمكن إسناد ذلك إلى « الطبيعة » التي لا مناص من تفسير عملها وآثارها ، مهما تنوعت التعابير عنها ، بالآلية أو العشوائية المجردة . وانتخاب الأصلح لا بد أن يعتمد على قانون يميز الأصلح عمن دونه ويعلل ذلك ويوجهه ، فعلى أي قانون تستند الطبيعة في انتخابها وما هو التعليل الذي هضمته الطبيعة لذلك ثم انطلقت متأثرة به ؟
4 - The process of selection is not an automatic movement, whether we consider it artificial or natural selection, but rather it is a means that aims at an end. And striving towards an end is considered one of the most complex operations of understanding and perception. So how can it be attributed to 'nature', which inevitably must be interpreted, however varied the expressions about it, as mechanical or pure randomness? Commentary
This passage presents the fourth argument against Darwinian natural selection. The author asserts that the process of selection, whether artificial (human-directed) or natural, is not an automatic, mindless movement. Rather, it is a means that targets a goal (ghayah). Striving towards a goal is one of the most complex operations of understanding and perception (a'qad 'amaliyyat al-fahm wa al-idrak). He then asks: how can such goal-directedness be attributed to 'nature', which must be interpreted—despite varying descriptions—as either mechanical or purely random? Next, he argues that the selection of the fittest requires a law (qanun) that distinguishes the fittest from the less fit, and that explains and directs the selection. He poses two rhetorical questions: what law does nature rely on in its selection? And what explanation has nature internalized in order to act accordingly? The implication is that nature, being blind and purposeless, cannot satisfy these requirements.

The Contradiction of Weak Organisms in Natural Selection
Buti poses a contradiction: if weak organisms are unfit, why did nature create them?

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's logical refutation of natural selection by pointing out the contradiction between nature creating weak organisms and then eliminating them.

Core Idea
Nature cannot both create the weak and eliminate them—that is self-defeating.

Buti challenges the internal consistency of natural selection. If nature is the agent of elimination, why does it produce what it later eliminates? This passage forces us to reconsider who—or what—is truly behind creation and destruction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic once to feel the rhetorical flow. Then read the translation.
2
Identify the two scenarios
Buti presents two alternatives: either nature creates and eliminates, or neither is up to nature. Notice the logical 'if...then' structure.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
3
Understand the contradiction
If nature eliminates the weak, it must be the cause of their weakness. But why create them weak first? That is inconsistent.
The contradiction is the core of the argument.
4
Consider the alternative
If creation is not nature's doing (i.e., God created), then elimination cannot be nature's doing either. This points to a higher power.
Buti uses this to defend teleology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن كان هذا الضعيف محكوماً عليه بالتخلف ، فالزوال ، لأنه ليس من صنف الصالح أو الأصلح ، فلماذا أوجدت الطبيعة هذا الذي تريد اليوم أن تقضي عليه أو تؤخره عن الركب ؟.. أما إذا قلنا أن أمر إيجاده لم يكن إليها ، فأحرى أن لا يكون إليها أيضاً أمر تهذيب الكون بإعدامه والقضاء على خطيئة وجوده
If this weak one is doomed to backwardness, then extinction, because it is not of the category of the good or the fittest—so why did nature create this which today it wants to eliminate or delay from the caravan? But if we say that its creation was not up to it, then it is even more fitting that the matter of refining the universe by exterminating it and eliminating the sin of its existence is also not up to it.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the logic of natural selection. Buti argues from within the Darwinian framework: if nature eliminates the weak and preserves the fittest, then why does nature initially produce weak organisms? This is self-contradictory. Alternatively, if creation is not nature's doing (i.e., if God creates), then nature cannot be the agent of elimination either. This exposes a flaw in attributing both creation and selection to purposeless nature.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Buti is rejecting all of evolution and natural selection outright.
Correction: Buti is not rejecting the observation of adaptation; he is pointing out an internal logical contradiction if nature is the sole agent. He leaves room for a creator.

Checkpoint

C) Weak organisms sometimes survive.

Key Takeaway
Buti's argument shows that natural selection cannot be a self-sufficient mechanism because it would contradict itself by creating what it eliminates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Why Haven't Animals Evolved Greater Intelligence?
Buti questions why natural selection hasn't produced greater intelligence in animals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti uses the uneven distribution of intelligence as a critique of natural selection and how Darwin acknowledged the difficulty.

Core Idea
If natural selection favors beneficial traits, why hasn't intelligence evolved more widely?

In this passage, Buti presents a pointed challenge to Darwinian evolution. He argues that if natural selection always drives toward fitness, then intelligence—a clearly beneficial trait—should be more widespread. He then cites Darwin's own acknowledgment of difficulty, revealing a crack in the theory's explanatory power.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
First, read the original Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the structure: Buti's question followed by Darwin's two responses.
Pay attention to the rhetorical force of the repeated 'why' questions.
2
Identify Buti's core argument
Buti assumes natural selection leads to beneficial traits. He then asks why intelligence—a beneficial trait—has not evolved in many animals. This is the logical challenge.
3
Examine Darwin's response
Darwin admits he cannot answer the question, first saying we should not expect a definite answer, later pleading ignorance of each species' history.
Buti uses this admission as evidence of the theory's limits.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this challenge undermines the claim that natural selection is the universal mechanism for all traits.
This connects to broader critiques of evolutionary theory.

: إننا لا ينبغي لنا أن نعثر على جواب محدود معين على هذا السؤال ، إذا ما عرفنا أننا لا جرم نعجز عن الإجابة على سؤال أقل من هذا تعقيداً

(۱)
